1. `a0 = -1; a1 = 2; a2 = 3; a3 = 0; a4 = 6`: Initialize variables `a0` to `a4` with the given values.
2. `a0 += a4`: Add `a4` to `a0`, so `a0` becomes `-1 + 6 = 5`.
3. `a1 = a3`: Assign the value of `a3` to `a1`, so `a1` becomes `0`.
4. `a1 = a3`: Again, assign the value of `a3` to `a1`, so `a1` remains `0`.
5. `a0 -= a2`: Subtract `a2` from `a0`, so `a0` becomes `5 - 3 = 2`.
6. `a1 -= a0`: Subtract `a0` from `a1`, so `a1` becomes `0 - 2 = -2`.
7. `a0 -= a1`: Subtract `a1` from `a0`, so `a0` becomes `2 - (-2) = 4`.
8. `a2 += a4`: Add `a4` to `a2`, so `a2` becomes `3 + 6 = 9`.
9. `a2 = a4`: Assign the value of `a4` to `a2`, so `a2` becomes `6`.
10. `a2 -= a4`: Subtract `a4` from `a2`, so `a2` becomes `6 - 6 = 0`.
11. `a4 = a4`: No change.
12. `a4 += a2`: Add `a2` to `a4`, so `a4` becomes `6 + 0 = 6`.
13. `a4 -= a3`: Subtract `a3` from `a4`, so `a4` becomes `6 - 0 = 6`.
14. `a0 = a2`: Assign the value of `a2` to `a0`, so `a0` becomes `0`.
15. `a0 -= a2`: Subtract `a2` from `a0`, so `a0` becomes `0 - 0 = 0`.
16. `a0 -= a3`: Subtract `a3` from `a0`, so `a0` becomes `0 - 0 = 0`.
17. `a3 += a0`: Add `a0` to `a3`, so `a3` becomes `0 + 0 = 0`.
18. `a2 -= a0`: Subtract `a0` from `a2`, so `a2` becomes `0 - 0 = 0`.
19. `a2 -= a4`: Subtract `a4` from `a2`, so `a2` becomes `0 - 6 = -6`.

Now, the final values of the variables are:

* `a0 = 0`
* `a1 = -2`
* `a2 = -6`
* `a3 = 0`
* `a4 = 6`

So, the value of `a4` at the end of the computation is `6`.

2. `a1 = -8`: Assigns the value -8 to the variable `a1`.
3. `a2 = 3`: Assigns the value 3 to the variable `a2`.
4. `a3 = 0`: Assigns the value 0 to the variable `a3`.
5. `a4 = 8`: Assigns the value 8 to the variable `a4`.
6. `a1 = a3`: Assigns the value 0 (which is the current value of `a3`) to `a1`.
7. `a0 += a3`: Adds 0 (the current value of `a3`) to `a0`, so `a0` now has the value -9 + 0 = -9.
8. `a1 += a1`: Adds 0 (the current value of `a1`) to itself, so `a1` now has the value 0 + 0 = 0.
9. `a1 = a0`: Assigns the value -9 (which is the current value of `a0`) to `a1`.
10. `a4 = a4`: Does nothing, as `a4` is already equal to 8.
11. `a4 -= a3`: Subtracts 0 (the current value of `a3`) from `a4`, so `a4` now has the value 8 - 0 = 8.
12. `a4 = a3`: Assigns the value 0 (which is the current value of `a3`) to `a4`.
13. `a2 = a2`: Does nothing, as `a2` is already equal to 3.
14. `a2 -= a3`: Subtracts 0 (the current value of `a3`) from `a2`, so `a2` now has the value 3 - 0 = 3.
15. `a3 += a4`: Adds 8 (the current value of `a4`) to `a3`, so `a3` now has the value 0 + 8 = 8.

20. `a4 -= a3`: Subtracts 16 (the current value of `a3`) from `a4`, so `a4` now has the value 16 - 16 = 0.

To solve this problem, you need to step through the code line by line and track the values of the variables. Here's one way to do it:

1. `a0 = -1; a1 = 6; a2 = 1; a3 = -6; a4 = -4`:
	* `a0 = -1`
	* `a1 = 6`
	* `a2 = 1`
	* `a3 = -6`
	* `a4 = -4`

	* `a1 = -1`

	* `a1 = -1 + -6 = -7`

	* `a3 = -6 - -4 = -10`

	* `a3 = -10 - -4 = -14`

	* `a3 = -14 + -4 = -18`

	* `a2 = -4 + -1 = -5`

	* `a2 = -5 + -5 = -10`

	* `a1 = -8`
16. `a0 += a2`:
	* `a0 = -8 + -10 = -18`
17. `a2 -= a4`:
	* `a2 = -10 - -8 = -18`
18. `a0 -= a4`:
	* `a0 = -18 - -8 = -26`

Now, the final values of the variables are:

* `a0 = -26`
* `a1 = -8`

1. > (increase)

4. - (subtract)
5. . (output)
6. , (input)
7. [ (loop)

<result>--------;</result>  The final value of a4 is -4.

Note: In Python, when you do a += b, it is equivalent to a = a + b and not a = a + b + a. Similarly, when you do a -= b, it is equivalent to a = a - b and not a = a - b - a.

Therefore, in the given code, a1 -= a3 means a1 = a1 - a3, and a1 += a3 means a1 = a1 + a3, and not a1 = a1 - a3 - a1 or a1 = a1 + a3 + a1.

Also, when a4 = 1 and a3 = 8, a4 -= a3 means a4 = 1 - 8 = -7, and a4 += a3 means a4 = -7 + 8 = 1, and not a4 = 1 - 8 - 1 or a4 = 1 + 8 + 1.

16. a2 = a4 = -30
17. a4 -= a2 = 41 - (-30) = 71
18. a3 -= a4 = -14 - 71 = -85
19. a2 -= a4 = -30 - 71 = -101
20. a3 += a3 = -85 + (-14) = -99
21. a4 = a2 = -101
22. a4 -= a3 = -101 - (-99) = -2

Therefore, the value of a4 at the end of the computation is -2.
</response>

a4=26
</ground-truth>

6. `a1 += a1`: a1 is incremented by a1, which is 0, so a1 remains 0.
7. `a0 = a3`: a0 is assigned the value -5.
8. `a0 += a3`: a0 is incremented by a3, which is -5, so a0 becomes -10.
9. `a1 += a4`: a1 is incremented by a4, which is 3, so a1 becomes 3.
10. `a2 = a2`: a2 remains unchanged at -2.
11. `a4 -= a3`: a4 is decremented by a3, which is -5, so a4 becomes -2.

20. `a4 = a4`: a4 remains unchanged at -7.
